And after the reduction of the cavity let it be placed on that cushion where there is inflammation and exudation from white pus, and be extended in a downward position, and the arm be suspended from the neck, and let it be left for some days.
And then it should be released; and therefore if the joint is formed in that location, then you release the ligament and leave it.
And if you see the joint not well strengthened, then iterate the poultice and ligament, and leave it for some days until it is extended; and then release it.
Moreover, if it happens to it that gravity affects the reduction of the joint, and its position is in movement, then administer moistening in bath and subtle friction and compression, until it is alleviated; or pause over the joint for a time, so it is a matter of much motion; and then bind it, and leave it over the bone day and night. And then immerse it in water, and when soaked, then friction the joint with tempered friction, and then iterate over it for a time, so it is a matter of much motion, one time, and the second, and the third. by means of bathing, when it is warm.
And if you wish, place your hand over that wet and flaccid groove at the edge and press strongly upon it; do this several times, for that is wet and you are restoring it to its proper state.
Chapter XXVIII.
For the treatment of shoulder dislocation, it is the joint where the arm meets the hand.
Shoulder of the hand is sometimes dislocated, and the reduction of this dislocation is easy. The opposite is true for other joints; however, more importantly, it is crucial that there be speed in the reduction when it is dislocated, before the area becomes inflamed or an abscess occurs.
And the reduction of the shoulder dislocation is that you place the patient's hand joint on a table and have them extend their arm. The physician then places their hand or palm over the vicinity of the joint and gently push it back into its proper place.
But rather it should be considered if the palm is already placed on the abdomen of the hand, then the patient pause the two of his hand on a table for extension and reduction; and if the dislocation is prior, then place the two of his hand, so that the position of the hand of the physician precisely on the table, in order that the hand of the doctor falls over that potential of the joint.
And so, if it returns quickly, that is good; otherwise, then strengthen that and apply a compress yielding to the abscess and leave it; and do not repeat this, for if you do not, do not suffer nor be unable regarding the reduction of it until days pass.
But rather the joint is to be reduced according to its tortuosity; and do not note any cause in the patient, but let the hand be softened and cannot strengthen any cause; then you know that the nerves are torn or cut, and then there is nothing in it but that it be strengthened with a cautery near the site and fortify it with this you confer some cause.
And since the gout has returned, then place over the compress which we have recommended, and let it be softened and strengthened for five days; and then release it and leave it, and exercise the hand of the patient.
If the movement in it is stopped and some gravity occurs, then loosen that with water cautery and some friction several times, until it is alleviated.
Capitol.xxix.
Of the cure of dislocation of the fingers.
In some cases, dislocate the fingers all at once.
And when one of those fingers is dislocated on the side of the palm or in its middle part, then hold the finger and push the dislocation back with your thumbs until it returns.
Then hold the base of the finger, suspend that part which was dislocated, and leave it for two days.
Then suspend that part and extend it until the finger is straight in that same day.
And when it is night, treat that part according to the aforementioned method, and do not cease to loosen and move it during the day, and treat it at night; do this for several days until it is straight.
And make it seem as if you are doing that, if it is dislocated in the abdomen by your hand, hold that part and do your first operation, until it is healed.
And make it seem as if you are doing that when it is dislocated in other parts.
Capitol.
For the treatment of dislocation of the second lumbar vertebra.
When a complete dislocation occurs in any of the lumbar or cervical vertebrae, and multiple vertebrae are displaced from their proper position, then there is no cure for that part, and death follows the patient.
The sign of this is that the patient's excretion is forcibly expelled against their will and they cannot retain it; often, several members of the patient or both hips or two arms of the patient, or one of those, are softened. Or a vertebra is displaced from its place, for multiple times it is displaced and multiple times the removal of those to four parts is performed.
Then it is already mended at the rear parts and named jaundice.
May the cure of it be that when you consider whether jaundice arises from retention, then in that case there is no cure and neither does it heal entirely.
May it be that in those cases where jaundice arises from congestion or percussion or semblance thereof, the Ancients have already detailed the methods of cure at length, in which the most returns to a prophecy; but I will now abbreviate that of which the few exceptions from too much of it are for my proximity to your understanding, by which I have herein expanded and formed various instruments from which I shall show and expand that.
And of those, only the one that arises in the two sides is cured as I recommend.
And the patient should be extended on his back as close to the wall as possible, and kept moistened with a cloth so that his feet are not irritated.
And place a straight stick, inserted into the ground at the end of the arm near its head, and another stick across his feet at the other end of the pole.
The minister should hold the stick, and it should not be fixed in the ground; another minister should hold the other end according to that form.
And wrap cloth around the head of the patient and tie it tightly with a ligature; extend the end of the ligature to the stick which is placed at the head, and tie that there. And wrap strong ligatures around the hips of the patient under his armpits, and support his legs; and adjust all the ligatures and tie those to the other stick which is placed at the feet.
And the minister should extend the ligature to the part of the stick, and do not move both sticks and the ligatures in which they are placed, but they should not be fixed exactly as we have said.
And the doctor places his palms on the spine with strength so that it returns, or he places one hand on a table and adjusts his feet on the table so that it returns.
And if it does not return in this way, then take a table whose width or length is about three braccia, and dig a hole in the wall where we said was near the hernia, in which between the ends of the table. And then place the greater part of the table on the spine, and the doctor places his feet on the other end. He presses well so that the spine is compressed and returns to its place.
And if you wish, open a turn which is revolved in your hand; and when you stand on the ground, place the base of the hernia at the heel of two sticks, whose length is that of one arm, and place its top at the heel of two sticks similarly positioned. The distance between each stick should be about one palm. In each stick, thread a cord, and secure each end firmly to the ground so it does not move.
And there should be a round stick for the turning, and it should be rotated in the two holes of the two sticks.
And at the end of it is a hole through which the stick passes, the length of which is one palm's breadth as it is rotated; and in the two other sticks, it is similar to that.
And then strengthen the ligaments you have stretched in the feet of the patient in the hole through which you place its head, and the ligaments you have stretched in the thighs of the patient in the turn where you place its feet.
And then you should place each turn and have a minister twist the turn with his hand, and the doctor straighten the spine as we have said.
And when the spine is returned and the area is straightened, then cover it with a paste of honey, and some wool; place a slice of table about three fingers or slightly wider in diameter, and the length should fit the area of the swelling, and on the part of the spine.
And then apply the honey which we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment until it is healed.
And if there is any danger at the site near the end of healing, then ensure that medicines that mitigate and relieve are administered for a long time through the table as we have recommended; and already a sheet of lead is applied in that location.
And sometimes accidents occur near the end of the vertebrae in the back, and are caused by that dislocation; and it is that bone for which you should already anticipate so that no suspicion arises about it with this medicine, as it will greatly affect you and cause death.
Chapter XXXI.
On the treatment of dislocated hip.
Know that the joint of the hip and the joint of the muscle should occur only due to dislocation, and not due to what occurs in other small joints with little movement and concavity.
And the joint of the elbow can be dislocated in four ways, namely dislocated to the internal parts, or to the external parts, or to the anterior parts, or to the posterior parts.
And primarily it is dislocated to the internal parts, and little to the anterior or posterior parts.
And the sign of dislocation to the internal parts is that when you adjust the healthy leg's knee against the sick one, the unhealthy knee becomes longer and more prominent than the healthy one. The sick leg cannot bend its foot; this is the place where you should cautery the felon, so that the head of the swelling is treated here.
And the sign of one who experiences dislocation to the external parts is that the symptoms of this condition are contrary to this accident.
And the sign of one who experiences dislocation to the anterior parts is that the knee swells according to the complement, but does not bend, and the pain in the kneecap persists. If it is forced further向前翻译这句话：“并且，对于那些希望将区块链技术应用于实际项目的人来说，了解如何选择合适的共识机制至关重要。”
And a sign of dislocation in the rear parts is that the hollow does not expand, nor can what is in front bend what is behind, and the thigh is shorter than the other, and the hip is softened, and the head of the thigh bone is displaced from that place.
The main sign of this dislocation is that you consider whether the dislocation is old, and if it is an ancient one, you have already treated it nearby by reducing it according to its position. However, this is not part of the entire treatment; then, you should not guess or form a presumption about it.
For the recent dislocation, which is one of the four species of dislocation, you should reduce it by returning the joint to its proper position and extending it to the internal and external parts, and manipulate it to the right and left sides, for it will naturally return and you will not need any other treatment.
Moreover, if it does not return in this manner, you should prepare a strong counterpoise and extend the thigh from the part behind or from its hands, or with linseed which is soaked over the hollow; another minister should stretch the hand above to try to grasp the tendons of the foot; then, strongly apply linseed on the back of the thigh, and have another minister hold the end of the linseed.
And it is the extension from his side inside to the angle at the side of the furcula, or from the back side to the side of the diaphragm.
And it is the extension of all those in one piece so that the patient's body is elevated from the ground and hangs suspended.
And this type of extension is special for all four.
And so, if the dislocation returns as we have said, it will be good; otherwise, for every type, it is necessary to do what I will say about its own treatment.
In the reduction of its own, when dislocated, and the dislocation is on the inside parts, ensure that the patient's body is revolved over their side; then place the bandages around the ribcage in that location where it lies between the head of the ribcage and the place where the angle is located; then extend the bandage above the part of the angle to the other side of the furcula.
And then another minister firmly takes hold of the thighs, and compresses the area around the bad hernia and extends it outward forcefully, for that which returns to its place.
And this species is of a gentle cure for which that member is reduced compared to other species.
But if you excuse yourself and do not follow the instruction for this cure, then carefully bind both feet of the patient together firmly, gently, over both the ankles and both the insteps.
And let the length of each be the quantity of four fingers, and let the bad hernia's flap be extended more than the other by the quantity of two fingers.
And then the hernia is suspended over the top of the stake, and it should be in the hand; let the length of it from the ground be the quantity of two braccia.
And command a strong youth to hold the thigh, and let him suspend it above the hernia, while another youth holds the thigh with great strength, for the joint returns to its place quickly.
In the proper reduction, when dislocation is at the upper part, guide the patient's leg according to what we have recommended in the healing of gout; and strengthen the ligament on the side of the affected thigh and on its knee.
And then place two poles to hold him, one on his foot and the other on his head; and let the poles be adjusted above the peg inserted under which wet cloths are wrapped, so that the patient is not damaged by the pole being between his thighs, for you need to maintain the extension of the parts left in place.
And then each minister extend to his part, and the doctor with his hand equalize the reduction according to the art.
When the dislocation is in the front parts, then you should slightly extend the thigh, and proceed according to this narrative about the leg; the doctor places the palm of his right hand on the popliteal region of the injured side, and then cuts with the other hand, and by that cut extends it to the front parts leaving it at the place of the kneecap.
If the dislocation is in the rear parts, then you should not extend the limb to the front, but elevate it above the ground; having done this, you should place it on a hard surface, as if it were similarly situated when the wide end is dislocated outward, as we have said regarding its position between two flat surfaces; and it should be placed with its face up and the ligaments extended, as we have said, not in any other manner.
A compress should be applied on the area where the joint is displaced.
Then, once the reduction is completed as it should be — and you notice the sign of the reduction, which is that you can extend both knees from the injured side, and when you see them equal and the limb expands its usual space, then you know that the member has been returned to its proper place — then adjust two cushions and wrap tightly with a bandage so that the width is not altered in any of the parts; adhere the limb to rest for three or four days.
And then compare one leg with the other, after separating the linen and wrapping.
When you see them equal in swelling, then know that the dislocation is healed, and then let the patient go.
And if you see any cause of swelling, then return and apply a poultice to that area, and extend it according to your first structure, and leave it for three days.
And then allow that area to gradually recover its mobility over each part for some days, until it is comfortable.
Capitol.xxxii.
On the treatment of dislocation of the shoulder.
The shoulder can be dislocated in three ways: it can be dislocated to the outer parts, to the inner parts, and to the back parts more than to the front parts; and it does not dislocate to the front parts.
And the sign of shoulder dislocation is that when you command the patient to apply their arm to their hip; then you know that the shoulder is dislocated.
And the restoration of all manners of it is that you make cease the labour straight, essay that it already extends its limb over this; attach your two hands to the face of it, and place his foot between your feet; then return his soles to your palms, and keep those between your thumbs on his soles with strength, and another minister extend his foot so that the sole returns to its place.
And the sign of its submission is that its limb attaches to the thigh with light, non-laboring effort.
And then apply that and attach the limb to the thigh, and place those constantly with a bandage for three or four days, and then remove those.
And do not use the labor of ambulation for some days until it is healed and comforted.
But if the reduction of it is excused to you, then administer strong extension to the limbs of which in the cure of the hip the preceding narration was given.
Capitol.xxxiii.
Of the cure of the dislocation of the ankle.
The ankle is sometimes reduced by a small movement, and sometimes dislocated according to the injury, and the dislocation of the ankle is performed either on the inner side or on the outer side.
And the sign of the dislocation of the ankle is that you see the ankle swollen from the side where it is dislocated.
More the cure of the reduction of the ankle is by gentle stretching, and it should be done with ease so that it returns to its normal position.
More in the cure of the ankle when it is dislocated according to the injury, make sure you straighten the limb properly, and have a strong and brave assistant at the back of the injured leg in the middle of the location.
And then place your right hand on the upper part of the foot, and with your left hand, hold the lower part of the foot at the location of the ankle.
And then draw the foot to your right hand, and towards the left side twice, and extend the left side; and push the foot's sole towards the right, let the leg bend as it works.
And do this twice according to how we have counted.
And then push the foot's sole towards the third bend of the leg, and you are at the knee.
So if it returns in one or two pushes according to this manner, and if you press the foot well, that is good; otherwise, then iterate the operation, for when it does not return.
But if the reduction is forbidden to you as we have advised, then place the foot on a board on the ground, and fix a stick firmly in the ground, and let it pass between the patient's thighs, and you have already wrapped a cloth around it so that the foot does not slip.
And then the minister holds their thighs, and another minister extends the foot with their hands or with the cloth tied around the back of the foot; and each minister extends themselves against the extension of their part, and the stick remains between the patient's thighs, holding that in place, so that the body of the patient is not drawn towards the left side as you maintain its extension.
And then the doctor equalizes the dislocation with his hands, while another assistant holds the healthy thigh at the place left vacant, so that the dislocation returns with ease.
And then as the dislocation returns and you declare the health of the reduction, then apply a strong plaster to it, and bind the foot with lint to the leg.
And beware of the nerves behind the tibia, for the lint over that area should not be strong and severely irritate it.
And then leave it for two or three days; and if the lint is moist, replace it.
And then remove the lint on the third day or the fourth, and prohibit the patient from walking for forty days. But if it is necessary for the patient to walk before that time, then there is no guarantee that the dislocation has not been dissolved and corrupted, and that it does not receive treatment.
And if an abscess occurs during the operation, then you should manage it at the place where we previously described in our narrative, in another location for treatment and fomentation, until it is ripe.
Chapter XXXIV.
For the treatment of dislocation of the toes in the feet.
Make sure that which is dislocated is reduced with slight extension; and what is not difficult, beforehand is easy.
But if the dislocation is in some of the toes of the foot, then you should place the patient's foot on the ground or on a table, and keep it thus as if walking.
Then place your foot on the ground, and keep your own foot above the area where the joints are located. Gently press that part with your foot using force, so that it returns to its proper position, and observe that it is reduced without any prominence appearing in that location.
Then place the abdomen of the foot on a table that can hold the entire foot, which should have two ends. Gently stretch and maintain this structure firmly for three days; then release it and allow the walking rest for several days until it is strengthened and its recovery is assured.
Chapter XXXV.
Of the types of displacement that occur due to sprain or fracture or any other cause.
When any of these causes occur, and you are involved in the treatment and restoration of it, mistakes can lead to death.
And for this reason, you must not presume in the treatment of it, but only someone who is skilled in the art, long accustomed to its use, merciful and pious; and who delays, neither burning nor presumptuous. And who uses at the beginning of medicines that lead to the cautery as much as necessary, leaving the cure to the divine judgment, rather than to him to whom you hope for a healing from loss, in alleviation of the disease, and in which any hope appears. And then strive to perform the reduction at the beginning of the cause, before it develops into an abscess that requires cautery.
And then, if the limb returns as we wish, proceed to administer treatment that leads to the cautery of the abscess and heals the sprain with what is suitable for it from the drying ointments.
And if dislocation is accompanied by a fracture and accidents in the separated bones, then you must realign their joints, doing so as we have said in simple ailments that precede these locations in the earlier parts.
And guard and avoid according to your virtue that of the instrument in the ways of fear according to which my preaching precedes you; for this is better to you from your Creator, and more permanent to your glory, and more greetings to your true self those in your time. Thus you finish the words of Albucasim perfectly of which may God bless. Amen.
